  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aa907de9-1dba-47d4-b7c9-78163f8b2649'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer373564267449219748">Santa Claus, my dear old friend, you are a thief, a traitor, a slanderer, a murderer, a liar, but worst of all you are a mockery of everything for which I stood. You have sung your last ho, ho, ho, for I am coming for your head. . . . I am coming to take back what is mine, to take back Yuletide . . .<br/><br/>—from <i>Krampus</i><br/><br/>The author and artist of <i>The Child Thief</i> returns with a moder</span>
  <span id="freeText373564267449219748" style="display:none">Santa Claus, my dear old friend, you are a thief, a traitor, a slanderer, a murderer, a liar, but worst of all you are a mockery of everything for which I stood. You have sung your last ho, ho, ho, for I am coming for your head. . . . I am coming to take back what is mine, to take back Yuletide . . .<br /><br />—from <i>Krampus</i><br /><br />The author and artist of <i>The Child Thief</i> returns with a modern fabulist tale of Krampus, the Lord of Yule and the dark enemy of Santa Claus<br /><br />One Christmas Eve in a small hollow in Boone County, West Virginia, struggling songwriter Jesse Walker witnesses a strange spectacle: seven devilish figures chasing a man in a red suit toward a sleigh and eight reindeer. When the reindeer leap skyward, taking the sleigh, devil men, and Santa into the clouds, screams follow. Moments later, a large sack plummets back to earth, a magical sack that thrusts the down-on-his-luck singer into the clutches of the terrifying Yule Lord, Krampus. But the lines between good and evil become blurred as Jesse's new master reveals many dark secrets about the cherry-cheeked Santa Claus, including how half a millennium ago the jolly old saint imprisoned Krampus and usurped his magic.<br /><br />Now Santa's time is running short, for the Yule Lord is determined to have his retribution and reclaim Yuletide. If Jesse can survive this ancient feud, he might have the chance to redeem himself in his family's eyes, to save his own broken dreams, . . . and to help bring the magic of Yule to the impoverished folk of Boone County.</span>

<div id="review_1455897857" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455897857" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455897857?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=amazing-artwork">amazing-artwork</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455897857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2760004493959186490">Sometimes I get really lucky with Amazon sellers, like when I got an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217274610?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>autographed copy of a Rainbow Rowell book</b>
</a>. This time, I got a poster with my order of Krampus:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448903051i/17204558._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Upon a little quick googling, it appears it originally came as a promotion through the <a href='http://www.sfbc.com/welcome/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Science Fiction Book Club.</a> While the artwork is detailed, the whole Christmas demon thing really isn't my aesthetic so I won't be hanging it up anytime soon.<br/><br/>Anyway, other than the artwork, I wasn't very impressed with this book.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449160208ra/17243639.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I guess I wanted s</span>
  <span id="freeText2760004493959186490" style="display:none">Sometimes I get really lucky with Amazon sellers, like when I got an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217274610?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>autographed copy of a Rainbow Rowell book</b>
</a>. This time, I got a poster with my order of Krampus:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448903051i/17204558._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Upon a little quick googling, it appears it originally came as a promotion through the <a href="http://www.sfbc.com/welcome/" rel="nofollow noopener">Science Fiction Book Club.</a> While the artwork is detailed, the whole Christmas demon thing really isn't my aesthetic so I won't be hanging it up anytime soon.<br><br>Anyway, other than the artwork, I wasn't very impressed with this book.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449160208ra/17243639.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I guess I wanted something more epic, something more fitting with the lore of yule and Krampus. What I got was Krampus is angry at Santa (who is really <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Baldr <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) and some trashy story. Maybe that's my fault for wanting a Christmassy story that feels like a classic; however, I felt that Krampus himself took a backseat to some mortal's mission to get back his wife. The artwork just feels like a mismatch for the overall story, so you'll be disappointed if you are judging this book by its cover. Brom may be a talented artist, but his storytelling doesn't live up to the expectations he's created at all.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2760004493959186490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1465721792" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18916690-krampus">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=horror">horror</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1465721792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3172768820150394371"><b>$1.99 on Kindle December 7, 2018!</b><br/><br/>Review also found at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://theparanormalpaladin.wordpress.com/'>https://theparanormalpaladin.wordpres...</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429315.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Ho ho ho, Merry Christmas!"</i>
</b><br/><br/>We've all been taught that Santa and Mrs. Claus look a little something like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429316.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>We've all been taught <b>wrong</b>. This is Santa:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429317.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And his wife:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429318.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Santa is really Baldr, an ancient Norse god and son of Odin. He was known for being all peace, love, and light, but was that the <i>real story</i> or was Baldr a great deceiver?<br/><br/>In this story, after Baldr dies in ancient times, he is reborn as</span>
  <span id="freeText3172768820150394371" style="display:none"><b>$1.99 on Kindle December 7, 2018!</b><br><br>Review also found at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theparanormalpaladin.wordpress.com/">https://theparanormalpaladin.wordpres...</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"Ho ho ho, Merry Christmas!"</i>
</b><br><br>We've all been taught that Santa and Mrs. Claus look a little something like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429316.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We've all been taught <b>wrong</b>. This is Santa:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429317.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And his wife:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429318.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Santa is really Baldr, an ancient Norse god and son of Odin. He was known for being all peace, love, and light, but was that the <i>real story</i> or was Baldr a great deceiver?<br><br>In this story, after Baldr dies in ancient times, he is reborn as Santa Claus. He takes over Yule and changes the holiday. Well, someone is not very happy about THAT.<br><br>Meet Krampus. Our villain, I mean hero, or is it anti-hero? Who knows, who cares. He's awesome.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429319.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Krampus has been imprisoned by Santa/Baldr for 500 years and has just gotten his freedom back, only to discover no one celebrates Yule anymore. No candy in shoes? No tributes? And where's his bag? Oh yeah, SANTA STOLE IT! The battle to bring back Yule is <i>on</i>. You're toast, Santa! <br><br>Here's Isabel and Jesse.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450455162i/17429320.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They are part of Krampus's Belsnickels. If Krampus bites you, you become a little bit demon. Your skin gets black spots and you grow claws, have heightened senses, live a really long time, the cold doesn't bother you, you don't need to eat as much, etc. But you have to obey his commands. So you're basically a slave, but hey, things could always be worse!<br><br>When we meet Jesse, he has lost his wife and daughter and is pretty much a loser. He can't keep a job, his truck barely works, and everyone hates him. He gets stuck doing jobs for The General, who runs the meth in town. And the police chief named Dillard wants him dead (and is sleeping with his estranged wife). He meets Krampus and ends up turning his life around. This is even a tale about FRIENDSHIP, people!<br><br>It's got a little bit of everything - horror and gore, comedy, mythology, fantasy... I love how the author wove ancient myths and paganism into the story. Flying yule goats instead of flying reindeer...Krampus is Loki's grandson...Yule was celebrated before Christmas existed and was about celebrating the winter solstice and the rebirth of the sun and was also connected to Odin and The Wild Hunt. It was about drinking, dancing, sex and partying! <br><br>It's really fascinating. The only reason I am not giving this 5 stars is because there was a little bit of issues with pacing at times. But overall, this was loads of fun and a perfect (for me) Christmas story.<br><br>The author, Brom, drew the pictures I posted above. He is amazing!!! So talented.<br><br><b>Original review</b>:<br><br>Loved it! What a great Christmas, er, I mean, <b>Yuletide</b> book! I'll post a review tomorrow, but I think I have found a new favorite author and I LOVED how he worked in ancient paganism and Viking/Norse gods and myths. It's got crazy hill-billy meth gangs, a Santa who looks like Odin, and Loki's grandson who looks like a demon with horns. Fun fun fun. Good for both horror and fantasy fans. Highly recommended! <br><br><b>Still $1.99 on Amazon Kindle: 17 DEC 2015.</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1405264175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1405264175" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1405264175?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18916690-krampus">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=on-hand">on-hand</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1405264175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13360490426883599947">Review also on<br/><a href='https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/2015/10/17/review-krampus/#more-3167' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png' width='350' height='117' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>"He's taking a switch<br/>To redden your backside<br/>Once he finds out you've been naughty, not nice<br/>The Yule Lord is coming to town..."</i><br/><br/>If you haven't heard of this Yuletide jingle, or of any Yule Lord, or of Yule for that matter, then like me, you probably grew up with a traditional sense of Christmas. You know, the one with Santa Clause , baby Jesus in the manger and Christmas trees drooping from the weight of baubles. If you did, then you wouldn't know anything about dear ol' Krampus,</span>
  <span id="freeText13360490426883599947" style="display:none">Review also on<br><a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/2015/10/17/review-krampus/#more-3167" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" width="350" height="117" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>"He's taking a switch<br>To redden your backside<br>Once he finds out you've been naughty, not nice<br>The Yule Lord is coming to town..."</i><br><br>If you haven't heard of this Yuletide jingle, or of any Yule Lord, or of Yule for that matter, then like me, you probably grew up with a traditional sense of Christmas. You know, the one with Santa Clause , baby Jesus in the manger and Christmas trees drooping from the weight of baubles. If you did, then you wouldn't know anything about dear ol' Krampus, the Yule Lord.<br><br>According to German folklore Krampus is a devilish creature who punishes misbehaving children with a switch from birch tree branches. If that doesn't freak you out, then you're probably lying because just look at him.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444830115i/16560258._SY540_.jpg" alt="Krampus the Yule Lord Brom" width="300" height="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Imagine waking up in the middle of the night to find that in your kitchen. I'd probably die pooping my jammies. Now onto the real review.<br><br>Jesse Walker's life is a mess of hillbilly drama. He is unable to support his wife and child from his singing in honkey-tonks and his troubles with law after getting mixed with the local druglord. He was contemplating on ending his sorry life but stops short when he sees Santa Clause chased by seven demons. After a scuffle in the sleigh between Santa Clause and the demons, a sack falls directly inside his trailer. Later, he discovers this sack is magical and can produce any toy he desires. This magical sack puts him in the path of the Krampus and his Belsnickels, and Santa Clause. To add to his troubles, he botches a drug run that makes him the most wanted loser in Boone County.<br><br>Krampus' Belsnickels get to Jesse first and he is dragged to meet the Yule lord. Krampus has been chained for half a millenium in a cave in the forgotten mountains of Boone County, West Virginia. After all the time he'd been shackled in the cave, the world has forgotten him and his traditions, which made him so weak to the point of non-existence. The only fuel driving him on is to exact revenge on Jolly ol' Santy Clause. He gets his chance when his Belsnickels bring him Jesse and the magical sack. After rounding up his Belsnickels and his remaining magic, Krampus is out to battle Santa Clause for Yuletide tradition supremacy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444830115i/16560259._SX540_.jpg" width="304" height="261" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Going into the novel, I was expecting peein-my-pants-because-I'm-too-afraid-to-go-to-the-bathroom-at-night kind of horror, jumpy horror as my co-blogger Vane calls it, because of that creepy cover. It isn't even the slow-burn kind of horror, it's not horror at all. It has horrific scenes and all, but not enough to classify this as one, so if you want to be scared shitless, this isn't the book for you.<br><br>What Krampus is --- a superb urban fantasy steeped in mythology. I love Krampus, the book and the character. He is a seven-foot, horned devil with the temperament of Sherlock Holmes and the dramatics of Tom Hiddleston's Loki, which made it very easy for me to root for Krampus. I expected him to be completely evil because of, again, the book cover, but he isn't. He is endearingly complex for his single-minded pursuit of ridding the world of Santa and all he stands for. He evokes the deities of the Greek myth, equal parts benevolent and malicious, with a capacity for human pettiness. He also has the best lines I've read in a long while.<br><br><b>
  <i>"It's time to be terrible."<br><br>“Shit spews from your lips as from the ass of a pig.”<br><br>“Burn? Smite? Punish? Why is your god so intolerant? So jealous? Why must there be only one god? Why is there not room for many?”<br><br>"The truth, the only one that matters, is that you are a buffoon, a nitwit, a puppet, a tick upon God's wrinkled scrotum."</i>
</b><br><br> <br>The origin stories of Krampus and Santa Clause might be a hit or miss for mythology aficionados.They were a hit for me. They were ambitious but brilliantly done, and they are not convoluted with complex magic systems or pseudo-science bullshit.<br><br>I also quite enjoyed Jesse's part of the story, there's a druglord, a murderer and corrupt law enforcement, to his chapters. He is the human element of this fantasy, the reader's reflection when faced with questionable reality, and I tell you, it was just as fun reading about his hillbilly drama as it was to read about seven-foot Krampus going at it with muscled and ripped Santa Clause.<br><br>This could've been easily a five star read, but I had to take away that last star because *gasp* it tried to teach us a moral lesson, to follow ones dreams, as subtly as being hit with a block of sharp cheddar to the face. If I wanted to read awkward self-love stories, I would've picked up a Coelho.<br><br>Overall, this was a wonderful read, Brom is an artist in every sense of the word. Like his provocative artwork, his writing is fantastically compelling. It drew me in without holding my hand, fed me a mash of lore and mythology which I happily devoured, wide-eyed with one hand out for more, and <s>best</s> <s>worse</s> best of all made me compassionate for the devil of Christmas.<br><br>--------------------------------------------<br>October 8, 2015<br><br><b>"It's time to be terrible."</b>- Krampus<br><br>Also, my new catchphrase when hitting them buffets!<br><br>FRTC<br>--------------------------------------------<br><br>Buddy Read with Paige Bookdragon</span>
  <a data-text-id="13360490426883599947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2218404434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2218404434" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2218404434?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062095664" href="/book/show/25143059-krampus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218404434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16383700703842462644">“Then let us go and be terrible.”<br/><br/>Aspiring musician Jesse is caught up in the war between Krampus the Yule Lord and Santa Claus on Christmas Eve.<br/><br/>Well, colour me impressed. I’m not entirely sure what I had expected from this book, but I certainly didn’t think Krampus would be such a complex, well-developed and, at times, sympathetic character! Brom effortlessly blends his storytelling capabilities with a lot of the mythology that surrounds the origins and history of Yuletide and Father Christmas. </span>
  <span id="freeText16383700703842462644" style="display:none">“Then let us go and be terrible.”<br /><br />Aspiring musician Jesse is caught up in the war between Krampus the Yule Lord and Santa Claus on Christmas Eve.<br /><br />Well, colour me impressed. I’m not entirely sure what I had expected from this book, but I certainly didn’t think Krampus would be such a complex, well-developed and, at times, sympathetic character! Brom effortlessly blends his storytelling capabilities with a lot of the mythology that surrounds the origins and history of Yuletide and Father Christmas. I learnt a lot about Norse mythology and Brom even includes a little section towards the end where he details some of the research he came upon whilst writing Krampus.<br /><br />It’s a fun read! And for the most part, it moves along at a consistent pace. Some parts did feel like they dragged on a tad, but I wonder if this is because I read it over quite a busy time and so I just felt like I was reading it forever? Brom is not only a talented writer, but also a fantastic illustrator and each chapter is accompanied with a delightfully devilish illustration.<br /><br />I absolutely loved the portrayal of Santa Claus as an evil character and the battle between himself and Krampus was quite enthralling. Brom creates a fantastic backstory explaining the antagonism between the two. It was sad when Krampus was trying to understand why Yuletide traditions have died out - but also fucking awesome when he goes on a gruesome killing rampage... didn’t I say he was complex?!<br /><br />All in all, a lot of fun, and one I’d suggest for reading over the festive period if you’re into mythology, fantasy and horror! What a combination of all three! 3.5 stars!</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer341332051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13490893472564466295">I started Krampus with low expectations. I'd been reading a lot for work lately, and didn't have the time to read something light and fun, but then a window appeared in my reading schedule right at the time this hit my desk. Thank you, Lord Krampus, for this early Yuletide blessing!!!<br/><br/>Krampus could be an adjunct book to the universe of American Gods. It's hillbilly noir crossed with Pan's Labyrinth. It's as Christmassy as you can get when your protagonist is out to murder Santa Claus (as it turns</span>
  <span id="freeText13490893472564466295" style="display:none">I started Krampus with low expectations. I'd been reading a lot for work lately, and didn't have the time to read something light and fun, but then a window appeared in my reading schedule right at the time this hit my desk. Thank you, Lord Krampus, for this early Yuletide blessing!!!<br /><br />Krampus could be an adjunct book to the universe of American Gods. It's hillbilly noir crossed with Pan's Labyrinth. It's as Christmassy as you can get when your protagonist is out to murder Santa Claus (as it turns out, that's pretty Christmassy). The funny is hilarious. The danger is real. And the violence is hilarious and real (I realize that makes me sound like a psychopath). <br /><br />I've read a lot of great books so far this year, but none of them have been as full of pure fun as Krampus.<br /><br />Make sure you read this if you like:<br />Neil Gaiman<br />Terry Pratchett<br />Glen Duncan<br />Charlaine Harris<br />Grimm (TV)<br />Once Upon A Time (TV)<br />Supernatural (TV)</span>

<div id="review_1836995363" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836995363" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836995363?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836995363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1920709831622764241">Krampus is coming to town!<br/><br/>Artist, writer and all around creepy cool cat Brom threw down some serious urban fantasy coin with this 2012 publication: and I was picking it up like a stoner on Doritos.<br/><br/>Seems that before Santa Claus started selling Coca-Cola back in the 30s, before even Charles Dickens was scaring the Scrooge out of Brits, hell before there was Brits – pagans were having fun with the Yule festival and at the center of the pre-historic party was a seven foot tall party ANIMAL named Kra</span>
  <span id="freeText1920709831622764241" style="display:none">Krampus is coming to town!<br><br>Artist, writer and all around creepy cool cat Brom threw down some serious urban fantasy coin with this 2012 publication: and I was picking it up like a stoner on Doritos.<br><br>Seems that before Santa Claus started selling Coca-Cola back in the 30s, before even Charles Dickens was scaring the Scrooge out of Brits, hell before there was Brits – pagans were having fun with the Yule festival and at the center of the pre-historic party was a seven foot tall party ANIMAL named Krampus. Brom recreates the Krampus myth and throws in some muy bueno twists to what is already a fun theme.<br><br>But this is not all comedy and laughs. Like Cormac McCarthy, Brom doesn’t play: you want gritty backwoods violence? You got it. Set in the Appalachian hills of West Virginia, this gets bloody and downright mean – but to his credit, Brom keeps the bad contextual and within the parameters of his story.<br><br>A very cool retelling of the Santa story, Brom has gone OLD school and tells of the origins of Krampus, the winter solstice festival, and a Santa that we only thought we knew. Truth be told, I’ve always been fascinated with how Christianity took over and adopted pagan festivals. Brom takes this theme and runs with it. Fans of Neil Gaiman's brilliant <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30165203.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a> will probably like this, I know I did.<br><br>Readers may also recall that Brom is the same guy who created a dramatic revisioning of the Peter Pan story in his 2009 novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief" title="The Child Thief by Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Child Thief</a>. Hey Brom! Here’s some more ideas:<br><br>Toyland Mafia<br>Mutha Gooz<br>Mary had a little lamb chop<br>Old McDonald had a body farm<br><br>Or any of Andrew Dice Clay’s poems.<br><br>Good fun.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481769927i/21453556._SY540_.jpg" width="353" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1920709831622764241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2629909766?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn❤Loves❤Listening #AUDIOBOOKADDICT" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn❤Loves❤Listening #AUDIOBOOKADDICT" href="/user/show/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict">Lyn❤Loves❤Listening #AUDIOBOOKADDICT</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18916690-krampus">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lyn❤Loves❤Listening #AUDIOBOOKADDICT by: </span>
      Stephanie's review
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=holiday">holiday</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=book-bargain-buy">book-bargain-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=amazing-narrator-performance">amazing-narrator-performance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=scribd">scribd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=violent">violent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42093375-lyn-loves-listening-audiobookaddict?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2629909766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13440448831275929608">Audio - Kirby Heyborne gets all the stars for his MASTERFUL performance. I was on a total listening high from page 1. I love it when an author picks the perfect narrator who embodies ALL the characters (and there were a lot in this book), and brings the story to life. The narrator totally did this book justice.<br/><br/>Story – 5 I’m now a Krampus fan stars<br/><br/>Looking at the cover you would think this was a story about an evil guy, but it wasn’t. Krampus is not evil. He’s been given a bad rap and is misunders</span>
  <span id="freeText13440448831275929608" style="display:none">Audio - Kirby Heyborne gets all the stars for his MASTERFUL performance. I was on a total listening high from page 1. I love it when an author picks the perfect narrator who embodies ALL the characters (and there were a lot in this book), and brings the story to life. The narrator totally did this book justice.<br /><br />Story – 5 I’m now a Krampus fan stars<br /><br />Looking at the cover you would think this was a story about an evil guy, but it wasn’t. Krampus is not evil. He’s been given a bad rap and is misunderstood. <br /><br />What’s the norm when people want you to believe there’s only one way of doing something?? In this case, celebrate Christmas?? Villainize the other tradition(s). <br /><br />In Brom’s book, Krampus and Santa are both decedents of Norse gods. During the course of Santa’s aka Baldr’s life, death and subsequent rebirth, he renounces his past and converts to Christianity. Krampus, on the other hand, embraces his roots and doesn’t want people to forget him or the Pagan ways celebrating the holidays.<br /><br />The tiny bit of knowledge I have of Norse Mythology comes from references in other books I’ve read and watching the Thor movies and Viking series. So what parts of Krampus’ story were in keeping with the actual Norse Mythology, I couldn’t tell you. It didn’t matter to me.<br /><br />While the story had all the elements of a horror story, I found it to be more thrilling and heartfelt than scary. LOVED IT!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13440448831275929608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1460228646" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1460228646" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460228646?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=movie-seen">movie-seen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=popular-with-friends">popular-with-friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=winter">winter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=holidays">holidays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1460228646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17942547610163116599">3.5<br/><br/><b>"Guard your dreams. Always guard your dreams.”</b><br/><br/>Brom is basically awesome - I read his reimagined version of Peter Pan last year in 'The Child Theif', and now found out he penned the Christmas lore dark drama/horror story Krampus. His prose is delectable. Bring on the legends!						<br/><br/>I don't know much about Christmas lore other than when I treated myself to the theatre to see Krampus when it was released during December. I'd seen the book pop up among friends and a horror reading group in my Good</span>
  <span id="freeText17942547610163116599" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br /><b>"Guard your dreams. Always guard your dreams.”</b><br /><br />Brom is basically awesome - I read his reimagined version of Peter Pan last year in 'The Child Theif', and now found out he penned the Christmas lore dark drama/horror story Krampus. His prose is delectable. Bring on the legends!						<br /><br />I don't know much about Christmas lore other than when I treated myself to the theatre to see Krampus when it was released during December. I'd seen the book pop up among friends and a horror reading group in my Goodreads feed for awhile before and after the movies release. To my delight, the movie was great fun and has turned into one of my top favorite for Christmas themed flicks to bring in the favorite season. While the movie was gifted with colorful humor, the book kept to its dark roots, although it snuck in some humor mainly in the forms of situational irony and the frustrated yule Lord screwing things up when he tries to get ahead. 						<br /><br />The point of view is mainly through a lead who encounters Krampus and then must use his resources to get back at a mini kingpin in his town who works with the local corrupted police force. Sometimes you have to side with the bad to battle the bad. Throw in some Christmas themed weapons like the magical santa sack that has more than toys at its bottom, and you get some Christmas themed fun on the morbid side. Santa may be a legend, and his henchmen of reindeers and other jolly souls isn't anything to laugh at, while poor Krampus is forced to bring along him limited resources of reluctant and semi self-hating slaved companions.						<br /><br />Krampus isn't the jolly old red-suited man who wants you to sit on his lap (at least not in an innocent way...), but you can't help but like him. He grew on me with his humor and his sense of honor of sorts. His motivations weren't wholly unpure, at least in his mind, and he does show compassion where its warranted. A dimensional villain who isn't actually a villain anymore, he's a sympathetic enough character who lets his wickedness reign in a couple of demented scenes.						<br /><br />There's mucho pagan legend and lore that predates the Santa legend, some of it passed down and some of it probably invented for the tale. On one hand dark and on the other hand meant to be a playful story that proudly shows its different. Jesse as the main is likeable but drifting through the book mainly for a human POV was a small surprise. <br /><br />I did like the twist with music at the end and how it plays with the creativity of the human heart. I think the theme is meant to keep the magic of love, creation, life and celebration alive. Krampus was shocked to find so many had turned away from the wonders of the world because they only cared about the luring gods of the pixels now - television sets, x-boxes, computers and phones. Pretty discouraging when even he gives up on the human race, but I dug the theme the author put in.						</span>
  <a data-text-id="17942547610163116599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1133469275" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133469275" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133469275?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062205254" href="/book/show/15819666-krampus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133469275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1912771117720849936">Other than a quick train through Boresville at around the halfway mark (about fifty pages right smack dab in the center of this book I found my interest drifting along with my eyelids) it's a damn-near perfect read. It has everything an man child like myself looks for in a piece of fiction. Viscera, plot, wild characters, action, humor, and redemption through trials. Yup, I dug the fuck outta this book.<br/><br/>Brom is an artist. Literally. He created the fantastic artwork that graces the cover of the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText1912771117720849936" style="display:none">Other than a quick train through Boresville at around the halfway mark (about fifty pages right smack dab in the center of this book I found my interest drifting along with my eyelids) it's a damn-near perfect read. It has everything an man child like myself looks for in a piece of fiction. Viscera, plot, wild characters, action, humor, and redemption through trials. Yup, I dug the fuck outta this book.<br /><br />Brom is an artist. Literally. He created the fantastic artwork that graces the cover of the book, as well as the imagery within, which is at times creepy but always gorgeous. I suggest getting a version with the artwork. I went all out and got the ebook with the audio book companion, and the experience was quite epic. Kirby Heyborne's narration is some of the best I've heard. He's better than Will Patton, and as good as Jim Dale and Andrew Macleod, at least in the range department. Everybody sounded different, and I love it when a narrator can pull that off. Feels like those old radio plays they used to air before television was a thing (no, I'm not old enough to remember them, but my grandparents had some of the recordings, and I was allowed to listen to them whenever I visited), only there's one guy instead of an entire cast. Kirby Heyborne's the real deal. If I'm preaching to the choir, I apologize, but I've never heard of the guy.<br /><br />I honestly did not expect to fall in love with Krampus, but I did. In my eyes, this book is a tragedy. Poor unloved, un-worshiped Krampus, whiling away the hours in his pit, shackled to the wall, plotting his revenge, sharpening his teeth and horns... Anyway, he's such a great character that I sometimes forgot he was a seven-foot-tall demon-thing. He was cool. I wanted to have a beer with him. Shoot the shit. Play toss-a-ring with his antlers.<br /><br />Finally, Krampus has one of the cooler catchphrases that I've come across, and it fits the tone of the novel exquisitely: "Time to be terrible!"<br /><br />In summation: I wouldn't recommend this to anyone who takes Christmas too seriously. This is a dark comedy, and it shits on numerous beliefs before focusing on one in particular. The magic is magical, the gore is gory, the humor is humory; what more could you ask for? Recommended around Krampusnacht, or if you prefer, Christmas. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1912771117720849936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sorbello" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello">Michael Sorbello</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453077205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4237823035145257292">Synopsis: Set in Appalachia, Krampus the Yule Lord is a twisted fairytale about a failed West Virginia songwriter named Jesse who gets ensnared on Christmas Eve in an eternal war between a not-so-saintly Saint Nick and his dark enemy Krampus, aka Black Peter, an ancient trickster demon.<br/><br/>Review: Completely ridiculous and laughably bizarre with lots of explicit violence and vulgar language to put the cherry on top of this hilariously gruesome Christmas adventure. Unlike most adaptations of this leg</span>
  <span id="freeText4237823035145257292" style="display:none">Synopsis: Set in Appalachia, Krampus the Yule Lord is a twisted fairytale about a failed West Virginia songwriter named Jesse who gets ensnared on Christmas Eve in an eternal war between a not-so-saintly Saint Nick and his dark enemy Krampus, aka Black Peter, an ancient trickster demon.<br /><br />Review: Completely ridiculous and laughably bizarre with lots of explicit violence and vulgar language to put the cherry on top of this hilariously gruesome Christmas adventure. Unlike most adaptations of this legend, Krampus is actually the good guy here (sort of) and Santa Claus is the cunning villain masquerading as a jolly and loving man that brings gifts to the world. Little did we know however, Santa has been hiding some pretty nasty secrets, including a history of slavery, brutal murder, unfair imprisonment and even harbors a bit of a messiah complex as he framed Krampus as an evil monster so that he could receive adoration and worship from those that didn't know any better in his place. What a manipulative psycho, right?<br /><br />Despite how freakishly bizarre and gruesome this story is, however, it is not without heart. There are many genuine moments of human suffering and triumph to tug on your heart strings. Even Krampus has a few heartwarming moments of grief and redemption as the main character Jesse helps to quell the hatred and desire for blood that he's harbored since the day Santa betrayed him many years ago.<br /><br />A very fun and wild book with just enough humanity to make you care about its characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4237823035145257292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer11104122130858345972">I've read a lot of books on Krampus in the past couple of years, but this one is my favorite by far! The illustrations by Brom were a fantastic addition (I purchased the print version....not sure if the e-version is the same).<br/><br/>This was an entirely different interpretation on the origins of Krampus than other authors had used. At points, (MANY), I found myself believing in the mistreatment of Krampus and wanting him to succeed, as this take certainly showed a divergent side to the lore. Humor was </span>
  <span id="freeText11104122130858345972" style="display:none">I've read a lot of books on Krampus in the past couple of years, but this one is my favorite by far! The illustrations by Brom were a fantastic addition (I purchased the print version....not sure if the e-version is the same).<br /><br />This was an entirely different interpretation on the origins of Krampus than other authors had used. At points, (MANY), I found myself believing in the mistreatment of Krampus and wanting him to succeed, as this take certainly showed a divergent side to the lore. Humor was infused in nearly every section--to some extent--while the raw brutality of a horror story was also present. A great mix for this story; one that certainly had me captivated from start to finish.<br /><br />Highly recommended!</span>

<div id="review_1854808592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1854808592" />
    <a title="Mel (Epic Reading)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7074816-mel-epic-reading"><img alt="Mel (Epic Reading)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487568293p2/7074816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1854808592?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel (Epic Reading)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel (Epic Reading)" href="/user/show/7074816-mel-epic-reading">Mel (Epic Reading)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7074816-mel-epic-reading?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7074816-mel-epic-reading?shelf=own-print">own-print</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1854808592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12292093010084937234">Sometimes we are very lucky to read an author that has thoughts and sentiments so close to our own it's as though we were cut from the same cloth. For me, at this moment, it is Brom. Ironically I met him many years ago (before he had written any books) at a comic expo where he was showcasing his Gothic art. Brom came across as a quiet and thoughtful person who didn't have much to say that wasn't shown in his art. I wish at the time that I met him I'd known how alike our thoughts might be! I also</span>
  <span id="freeText12292093010084937234" style="display:none">Sometimes we are very lucky to read an author that has thoughts and sentiments so close to our own it's as though we were cut from the same cloth. For me, at this moment, it is Brom. Ironically I met him many years ago (before he had written any books) at a comic expo where he was showcasing his Gothic art. Brom came across as a quiet and thoughtful person who didn't have much to say that wasn't shown in his art. I wish at the time that I met him I'd known how alike our thoughts might be! I also wish I had talked to him more to get a real sense of him as a person. <br /><br />I intentionally savoured this book. I read it slowly, thoughtfully and made it last. I haven't done this with a book in a long time and didn't plan to do it with Krampus; but I just didn't want this amazing story to end too soon. This book had a real voice to it that sang to my soul and (as cheesy as this may sound) reminded me of who I truly am. <br /><br /><b>Krampus</b><br />As a raised Christian, converted Wiccan (15+ years ago); I really wanted to read a book about Christmas that wasn't about Christmas being wonderful; but instead was about how it ripped off Yule. I could not have asked for a better book than Krampus to do this. The devil figure of Krampus, while largely unknown in North America, is prevalent in European history. He beats children who don't behave or pay Yuletide tribute to him and blesses those children who do pay tribute with gold coins. It's all or nothing with this demon. Yule falls on the Winter Solstice (Dec 21) and was practiced long before Christmas existed (a fact many like to forget or look over to make their holiday seem more sacred than it might otherwise appear). <br />I loved Brom's use of Asgard, Loki and other ancient gods to bring together the backstory of Krampus, Santa and others. It gave a solid backing (with little explanation needed) to base these mythical characters on. Of course you didn't need to have a huge imagination to see the Krampus that Brom envisioned as there are gorgeous full colour, and pencil sketches in this book that show our characters at different levels of detail. The artwork really adds to the telling of this story and I was thrilled at every chapter break to have a new pencil sketch to look at. <br /><br /><b>The Story Itself</b><br />Plot wise Krampus (the book) is quite simple. Krampus (the character) has escaped a thousands of years prison that Santa Claus put him in and is out to destroy Christmas and bring back the traditions and beliefs of Yule. For those not aware many of the items used in popular Christmas traditions today originated from Yule; including decorating a fir tree and using shoes or stockings to fill with treats. <br />Brom has created a story about (mostly) awful humans and their struggle to survive. Without Krampus' involved at all the story of the humans is interesting enough. Add in some demon slaves (Belsnickel's), magic sand, a flying sleigh and a powerful sack of items (not always toys); suddenly you have a story that is complex, yet easy to follow. I loved the plot so much in Krampus. It drives forward our characters and forces them to make decisions throughout the book. This is not a passive plot by any means. Brom ensures the plot is forced forward whether our characters are ready or not. <br /><br /><b>Is it horror?</b><br />I've read in a few places that people are unsure about picking up Krampus because they believe it might be too gory or involve child abuse. Let me dissuade you from these thoughts, while many deaths happen (and a lot of blood is spilled) there is no more violence or graphic nature to this book than in your average CSI episode or best selling thriller. A few moments might be a bit much for some but they are fleeting and so short it's hard to even remember them amongst all the other details provided. <br />This is not so much horror as it is gothic fantasy. There is a darkness to the entire book; but not one that fits the horror genre. Instead Krampus focuses on the horrors of our world that we have become immune to. Examples like alcoholism, strip mining, mindless video gaming and other 'normal' activities that most of society today has accepted are the true horrors. You may come away from this book feeling like your outlook on the world has changed some; but it won't be because you're horrified by gore, instead it will be because you're horrified by what we've allowed our society to become. <br /><br /><b>Nature and Respect</b><br />At it's core Krampus is really about the balance between nature and humans. We are a parasite to our planet (like it or not). We've created holidays and mass marketing to support our consumerism and endorse the greed that humans are naturally subject to. As a Wiccan I found that Brom really spoke to my heart about things I wish I could change in today's society. And even if I can't make any more of a dent in some things than I already am; it's nice to know that someone else in the world understands that what we've done is wrong; even if irreparable. We've lost respect for the 'old ways' and forgotten why they were important (and still maybe should be). Krampus reminds us of these lost traditions and thoughts in different ways and at different points during the book. There is no one moral at the end; instead values are exquisitely threaded throughout the book so that you don't ever feel overwhelmed by it; but also so you cannot close your mind to accepting the reality of our circumstances. <br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br />There are so many more things I could say about this book! Adorable characters like Isabel and her panda hat stand next to the ancient Shawnee who are more demon than human in some ways. Brom brings all our characters together by having them affected by one common thread, Krampus has influenced them in some way, shape or form. It's brilliant the way Brom has allowed everyone to find a small part of themselves in each of the Belsnickel's (Krampus' followers/slaves). <br /><br />If you love Christmas and Santa Claus this is maybe not the book for you; unless you want to learn a little more about Yule. Brom has included an afterword talking of some of his research and narrative choices that may not be as accurate as they could be or evolved as he wrote. I really appreciated reading this. I knew from the introduction that Brom had to have done research but for anyone that is unsure or doesn't know many of these stories this afterword is reassurance that some thought was put into the scenarios, characters and rituals chosen. <br />I could easily see myself reading this book every few years in December. A nice reminder that there are others out there that dislike Christmas as much as I do and for similar reasons. <br /><br />If you are looking for a gothic read that forces you to look at the world for what it is then I highly recommend Krampus. If you're nervous about it because it is not a 'happily ever after' setting then I recommend reading the first 5 or so chapters to see if it's for you. I think almost everyone will be hooked by that point and unable to put this brilliant book down until the last page. So you better not pout, you better not cry because Krampus is coming to town and he will judge your loyalty to him and his Yuletide traditions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12292093010084937234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1251905067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251905067" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251905067?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-but-not-quite-there-yet">great-but-not-quite-there-yet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bittersweet-ending">bittersweet-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=blood-guts-n-gore">blood-guts-n-gore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=creepy-yet-entertaining">creepy-yet-entertaining</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251905067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13258173542749374058"><blockquote>
  <i>"Santa Claus wiped the blade clean of blood, replaced it in his sheath. [...] 'Krampus, my dear old friend, you will pay. Your death is mine and I intend to make it a terrible one."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>He sees you when you're sleeping. Oh, yes, he does.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479555587ra/21205432.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I gave the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief' title='The Child Thief by Brom' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Child Thief</a> five stars off the bat last year and was really looking forward to diving into another one of Brom's novels. He's such a gifted writer, on par with the King (Stephen) himself, and it's a shame his work isn't better known.<br/><br/>All I know about</span>
  <span id="freeText13258173542749374058" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Santa Claus wiped the blade clean of blood, replaced it in his sheath. [...] 'Krampus, my dear old friend, you will pay. Your death is mine and I intend to make it a terrible one."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>He sees you when you're sleeping. Oh, yes, he does.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479555587ra/21205432.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I gave the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief" title="The Child Thief by Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Child Thief</a> five stars off the bat last year and was really looking forward to diving into another one of Brom's novels. He's such a gifted writer, on par with the King (Stephen) himself, and it's a shame his work isn't better known.<br><br>All I know about Krampus is from that Supernatural Christmas episode. He is Santa's evil twin and punishes the wicked during Christmas. Brom's Krampus is a bit like that. He's a pagan Norse god and demands sacrifices every winter solstice. Santa has chained him up for centuries, but he manages to escape with the help of his slave-elves and our down-on-his-luck protagonist, and goes looking for revenge. <br><br>And spread a little Yule cheer.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It's time to be terrible."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Like Peter from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief" title="The Child Thief by Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Child Thief</a>, <b>Krampus is an antihero.</b> He's infuriated the world has forgotten him and the Yule Festival and not above spilling a little blood in his quest to return to power. He threatens to beat little kids with birch rods if they don't believe. At the same time, he's capable of great good. He's confused and lost in a time where pagan gods no longer hold sway. Imagine your elderly grandma on a highway. That's what it's like for him.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Other than his thumbs, the boy barely moved the whole time, staring glassy-eyed, his mouth half-open, looking like a lobotomy patient.<br><br>'He is bewitched.' Krampus strolled purposefully across the room, right up to the screen and smashed it in with his fist.<br><br>The boy clutched the cake controller to his chest and froze, his eyes threatening to burst from his head. Krampus leaned over to the boy. 'You are free. The world is now yours. Go take it."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>There's also a <b>heavy religious theme</b> since Christianity and pagan religions don't exactly have the best relationship. It does a great job criticizing religion while showing things back then aren't all that great either. Both have their good points. Krampus represents nature and energy. Christianity represents charity.<br><br>Despite all the good things going for it, I didn't like it as much as The Child Thief. The plot is a little <b>run-of-the-mill Hollywood.</b> You have the loser dad with his estranged wife and cute kid. The wife has a new boyfriend who's beefy and successful and belittles the hero. Bad Thing happens to his family and Dad saves the day, all while recovering his self-esteem and loses ten pounds. Closing shot: happy reunion.<br><br>Consider gifting this as a Christmas present though. It'll certainly get you noticed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479555587ra/21205433.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13258173542749374058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1423692694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423692694" />
    <a title="Tyler J Gray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6296289-tyler-j-gray"><img alt="Tyler J Gray" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570181254p2/6296289.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4293662562629867719">Re-read December 2018<br/><br/>I was really enjoying this book, then closer the end I got to a part (I didn't remember a THING from reading it 3 years ago!) that had me going "Seriously past me? WTF were you on? What were you thinking? Saying this is a favorite awesome book and 5 stars?!" Then the very ending happened, and i'm like "Oh...I see" and past me is now doing a jig and saying "hahahaha I told you I told you!" but as silly as that sounds, that is obviously a good thing. Lesson learned: Trust past</span>
  <span id="freeText4293662562629867719" style="display:none">Re-read December 2018<br /><br />I was really enjoying this book, then closer the end I got to a part (I didn't remember a THING from reading it 3 years ago!) that had me going "Seriously past me? WTF were you on? What were you thinking? Saying this is a favorite awesome book and 5 stars?!" Then the very ending happened, and i'm like "Oh...I see" and past me is now doing a jig and saying "hahahaha I told you I told you!" but as silly as that sounds, that is obviously a good thing. Lesson learned: Trust past me. Past me knew what I was talking about. 5 stars, again. Krampus is coming to town! Also, finishing this on Yule so Merry Yule! :)<br />____________________<br /><br />(First Read)<br /><br />This was an amazing book! I recommend keeping an open mind while reading it, as it has much religion (christian and pagan) in it. It doesn't appear to me to say either is bad or good. They both have their stuff, good and bad. <br /><br />It is a horror story. It has violence, blood/gore, death, drugs and crime in it. <br /><br />It had me engaged the entire time and my emotions went up and down, and there were tears (of both joy and sorrow). The ending had me with no idea how I should feel at first but man I loved that ending! I loved the entire book! I've annotated, highlighted and used post it tabs, the book all over the place!<br /><br />This has GOT to go on my favorites shelf! The afterword as well explains so much real life history. Oh and you can't forget the wonderful illustrations! This was my first book by Brom and I was not disappointed!</span>

<div id="review_1528278842" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528278842" />
    <a title="Cameron Chaney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40648249-cameron-chaney"><img alt="Cameron Chaney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596633386p2/40648249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528278842?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cameron Chaney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cameron Chaney" href="/user/show/40648249-cameron-chaney">Cameron Chaney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528278842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5150295655659501204">Okay, wow. I don't know how I managed to completely forget I even read this book, but I guess I did.<br/><br/>I read this during Christmas (obvs) but after finishing it, it's like it disappeared from my mind. I didn't forget what happened in the story, I just didn't think about it after it was over... does that make sense? *shrugs* Anyway, I was just now lying in bed trying to get to sleep, when a random thought hit me: "Woah, I never even marked Krampus as read." Does that mean Krampus is a bad book if I</span>
  <span id="freeText5150295655659501204" style="display:none">Okay, wow. I don't know how I managed to completely forget I even read this book, but I guess I did.<br /><br />I read this during Christmas (obvs) but after finishing it, it's like it disappeared from my mind. I didn't forget what happened in the story, I just didn't think about it after it was over... does that make sense? *shrugs* Anyway, I was just now lying in bed trying to get to sleep, when a random thought hit me: "Woah, I never even marked Krampus as read." Does that mean Krampus is a bad book if I forgot it so quickly? Well, no... but it's definitely a difficult book to rate.<br /><br />From seeing the cover and illustrations, plus reading the synopsis, I was very excited to start it, expecting a dark horror-fantasy with plenty of magic and epicness (not a word, I know). But it just wasn't what I hoped for.<br /><br />For one, it's not horror. At all. And while it is dark in its own way, it never really shocked me or gave me chills. If anything, it's darkness leaned toward the comedic, sometimes goofy. Dark humor is fine, but it wasn't what I was looking for when I picked up this book. Whimsical, yes. But goofy? No.<br /><br />Another thing is that the story focused a lot more on the problems of Jesse, the MC, and less on the war between Krampus and Santa Claus. I wanted more build-up of that battle, but a lot of time was spent with Jesse and blah. There were some good moments involving Jesse and his struggles to win back his family , but it could have been cut down with more Krampus/Claus in its place.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I still enjoyed the book enough. The mythology involving Krampus and Santa Claus was good, and took the story in an interesting direction. It was also an entertaining read, so I was never really bored. I was just a little let down by the tone. Had the book been more like it's illustrations, it would have gotten an A+ from me.<br /><br />Now, if you'll excuse me, I'm going to go back to bed. I don't think writing a review on my phone in the dark is the best for one's eyes. 'Kay, bye.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5150295655659501204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83144-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479156984p2/83144.jpg" /></a>
